For the company, see <a href="/wiki/DeepSeek" title="DeepSeek">DeepSeek</a>.</div>

</div></link></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a class="external text" href="https://chat.deepseek.com/" rel="nofollow">chat<wbr/>.deepseek<wbr/>.com</a></span> <span class="mw-valign-text-top noprint" typeof="mw:File/Frameless"><a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q132324293#P856" title="Edit this at Wikidata"><img alt="Edit this at Wikidata" class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/20px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png" width="10"/></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>DeepSeek</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Chatbot" title="Chatbot">chatbot</a> created by the Chinese artificial intelligence company <a href="/wiki/DeepSeek" title="DeepSeek">DeepSeek</a>.
</p><p>Released on 10 January 2025, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DeepSeek-R1" title="DeepSeek-R1">DeepSeek-R1</a> surpassed <a href="/wiki/ChatGPT" title="ChatGPT">ChatGPT</a> as the most downloaded <a href="/wiki/Freeware" title="Freeware">freeware</a> app on the <a href="/wiki/App_Store_(Apple)" title="App Store (Apple)">iOS App Store</a> in the United States by 27 January.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metz-2025b_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Metz-2025b-2"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> DeepSeek's success against larger and more established rivals has been described as "upending AI"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metz-2025b_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Metz-2025b-2"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and initiating "a global AI <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">space race</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zahn_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zahn-3"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> DeepSeek's compliance with Chinese government <a href="/wiki/Chinese_censorship_abroad" title="Chinese censorship abroad">censorship policies</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Mass_surveillance_in_China" title="Mass surveillance in China">data collection practices</a> have also raised concerns over privacy and information control in the model, prompting regulatory scrutiny in multiple countries. However, it has also been praised for its open weights and infrastructure code, energy efficiency and contributions to the <a href="/wiki/Open-source_artificial_intelligence" title="Open-source artificial intelligence">open-source community</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc">
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On 10 January 2025, DeepSeek released the chatbot, based on the DeepSeek-R1 model, for <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>. By 27 January, DeepSeek-R1 surpassed <a href="/wiki/ChatGPT" title="ChatGPT">ChatGPT</a> as the most-downloaded <a href="/wiki/Freeware" title="Freeware">freeware</a> app on the <a href="/wiki/App_Store_(Apple)" title="App Store (Apple)">iOS App Store</a> in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metz-2025b_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Metz-2025b-2"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> which resulted in an 18% drop in Nvidias share price.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Picchi_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Picchi-7"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> After a "large-scale" <a href="/wiki/Cyberattack" title="Cyberattack">cyberattack</a> on the same day disrupted the proper functioning of its servers, DeepSeek limited its new user registration to phone numbers from mainland China, email addresses, or Google account logins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 3 April 2025, in collaboration with researchers at <a href="/wiki/Tsinghua_University" title="Tsinghua University">Tsinghua University</a>, DeepSeek published a paper unveiling a new model that combines the techniques generative reward modeling (GRM) and self-principled critique tuning (SPCT). The resulting model is referred to as DeepSeek-GRM. The goal of using these techniques is to foster more effective inference-time scaling within their LLM and chatbot services. Notably DeepSeek has said that these new models will be released and made open source.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 April 2025, Deepseek released its math-focused Artificial Intelligence Model named "DeepSeek-Prover-V2-671B". This Model is useful for formal theorem proving and mathematical reasoning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Usage">Usage</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Usage"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>DeepSeek can answer questions, solve logic problems, and write computer programs on par with other chatbots, according to benchmark tests used by American AI companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metz-2025b_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-Metz-2025b-2"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Users can access the chatbot for free through the official DeepSeek website or mobile application, without limitation on the number of queries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeepSeekPriceComparison_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeepSeekPriceComparison-14"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> DeepSeek also offers access to the <a href="/wiki/DeepSeek#R1" title="DeepSeek">R1</a> and <a href="/wiki/DeepSeek#V3" title="DeepSeek">V3</a> models that power the chatbot via an <a href="/wiki/API" title="API">API</a> with a usage-based pricing model.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> This modality is primarily targeted towards developers and businesses. As of February 2025, API usage is priced at approximately $0.55 per million input tokens and $2.19 per million output tokens, making it less expensive than some competing services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeepSeekPriceComparison_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-DeepSeekPriceComparison-14"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Operation">Operation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Operation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>DeepSeek-V3 uses significantly fewer resources compared to its peers. For example, whereas the world's leading AI companies train their chatbots with <a href="/wiki/Supercomputer" title="Supercomputer">supercomputers</a> using as many as 16,000 <a href="/wiki/Graphics_processing_unit" title="Graphics processing unit">graphics processing units</a> (GPUs), DeepSeek claims to have needed only about 2,000 GPUsnamely, the H800 series chips from <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">Nvidia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deng,_Chengqi-2024_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deng,_Chengqi-2024-16"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It was trained in around 55 days at a cost of US$5.58 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deng,_Chengqi-2024_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Deng,_Chengqi-2024-16"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> which is roughly one-tenth of what tech giant <a href="/wiki/Meta_Platforms" title="Meta Platforms">Meta</a> spent building its latest AI technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metz-2025b_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-Metz-2025b-2"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Reactions">Reactions</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Reactions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>DeepSeek's success against larger and more established rivals has been described as "upending AI",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metz-2025b_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-Metz-2025b-2"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> constituting "the first shot at what is emerging as a global AI space race",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zahn_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zahn-3"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and ushering in "a new era of AI <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/brinkmanship" title="wikt:brinkmanship">brinkmanship</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-17"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Challenge_to_US_AI_dominance">Challenge to US AI dominance</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Challenge to US AI dominance"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>DeepSeek's competitive performance at relatively minimal cost has been recognized as potentially challenging the global dominance of American AI models.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Various publications and news media, such as <a href="/wiki/The_Hill_(newspaper)" title="The Hill (newspaper)"><i>The Hill</i></a> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a>,</i> have described the release of the R1 chatbot as a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sputnik_moment" title="Sputnik moment">Sputnik moment</a>" for American AI,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Milmo-2025_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Milmo-2025-20"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoskins_RJ_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hoskins_RJ-21"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> echoing <a href="/wiki/Marc_Andreessen" title="Marc Andreessen">Marc Andreessen</a>'s view. OpenAI wrote a letter to the Office of Science and Technology Policy (OSTP), in March 2025, citing issues concerning a possibility that Deepseek could manipulate responses to cause harm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-22"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Chinese_perspective">Chinese perspective</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Chinese perspective"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>DeepSeek's founder <a href="/wiki/Liang_Wenfeng" title="Liang Wenfeng">Liang Wenfeng</a> has been compared to OpenAI CEO <a href="/wiki/Sam_Altman" title="Sam Altman">Sam Altman</a>, with <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> calling him the Sam Altman of China and an evangelist for AI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Chinese <a href="/wiki/State_media" title="State media">state media</a> widely praised DeepSeek as a national asset.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On 20 January 2025, China's Premier <a href="/wiki/Li_Qiang" title="Li Qiang">Li Qiang</a> invited Wenfeng to his symposium with experts and asked him to provide opinions and suggestions on a draft for comments of the annual 2024 government work report.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On 20 February 2025, Wenfeng met with <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a>, who encouraged government officials to experiment with DeepSeek.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-22"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Government officials responded to Xi's approval of the chatbot by reportedly using it to draft legal judgements, propose medical treatment plans, and analyze surveillance videos to search for missing persons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-:2-22"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Performance_and_success">Performance and success</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Performance and success"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Leading figures in the American AI sector had mixed reactions to DeepSeek's performance and success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DSCI_1_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-DSCI_1-27"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Microsoft CEO <a href="/wiki/Satya_Nadella" title="Satya Nadella">Satya Nadella</a> and Altmanwhose companies are involved in the United States government-backed "<a href="/wiki/Stargate_LLC" title="Stargate LLC">Stargate Project</a>" to develop American AI infrastructureboth called DeepSeek "super impressive".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Various companies including <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Web_Services" title="Amazon Web Services">Amazon Web Services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stripe,_Inc." title="Stripe, Inc.">Stripe</a> are seeking to use the model in their program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> When American President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> announced The Stargate Project, he referred to DeepSeek as a wake-up call<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and a positive development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Milmo-2025_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Milmo-2025-20"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoskins_RJ_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hoskins_RJ-21"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Other leaders in the AI field, howeverincluding <a href="/wiki/Scale_AI" title="Scale AI">Scale AI</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Alexandr_Wang" title="Alexandr Wang">Alexandr Wang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthropic" title="Anthropic">Anthropic</a> cofounder and CEO <a href="/wiki/Dario_Amodei" title="Dario Amodei">Dario Amodei</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a>have expressed skepticism of the app's performance or of the sustainability of its success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DSCI_1_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-DSCI_1-27"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Stock_market_implications">Stock market implications</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Stock market implications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><p>
DeepSeek's optimization of limited resources has highlighted potential limits of United States sanctions on China's AI development, including export restrictions on advanced AI chips to China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scmp_1_January_2025_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-scmp_1_January_2025-36"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The success of the company's AI models consequently "sparked market turmoil"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and caused shares in major global technology companies to plunge on 27 January 2025: Nvidia's stock fell by as much as 1718%,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> as did the stock of rival <a href="/wiki/Broadcom" title="Broadcom">Broadcom</a>. Other tech firms also sank, including <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> (down 2.5%), <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>'s owner <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_Inc." title="Alphabet Inc.">Alphabet</a> (down over 4%), and Dutch chip equipment maker <a href="/wiki/ASML_Holding" title="ASML Holding">ASML</a> (down over 7%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoskins_RJ_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hoskins_RJ-21"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> A global sell-off of technology stocks on <a href="/wiki/Nasdaq" title="Nasdaq">Nasdaq</a>, prompted by the release of the <code>R1</code> model, led to record losses of about $593billion in the market capitalizations of AI and computer hardware companies;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and by the next day a total of $1 trillion of value was wiped from American stocks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Milmo-2025_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-Milmo-2025-20"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></p><figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a class="mw-file-description" href="/wiki/File:Deepseek_login_error.png"><img class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Deepseek_login_error.png/330px-Deepseek_login_error.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Deepseek_login_error.png/500px-Deepseek_login_error.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Deepseek_login_error.png/960px-Deepseek_login_error.png 2x" width="310"/></a><figcaption>The login error given by DeepSeek on 28 January 2025 following a cyberattack</figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Concerns">Concerns</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Concerns"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Distillation">Distillation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Distillation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>DeepSeek has been reported to sometimes claim that it is ChatGPT.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> OpenAI said that DeepSeek may have "inappropriately" used outputs from its model as training data in a process called <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_distillation" title="Knowledge distillation">distillation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> However, there is currently no method to prove this conclusively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Censorship">Censorship</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Censorship"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chinese_censorship_abroad" title="Chinese censorship abroad">Chinese censorship abroad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Censorship_in_China" title="Censorship in China">Censorship in China</a></div>
<p>DeepSeek's compliance with Chinese government <a href="/wiki/Chinese_censorship_abroad" title="Chinese censorship abroad">censorship policies</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Mass_surveillance_in_China" title="Mass surveillance in China">data collection practices</a> have raised concerns over privacy and information control in the model, prompting regulatory scrutiny in multiple countries.
</p><p>Reports indicate that it applies content moderation in accordance with the government's "<a href="/wiki/Public_opinion_guidance" title="Public opinion guidance">public opinion guidance</a>" regulations, limiting responses on topics such as the <a href="/wiki/1989_Tiananmen_Square_protests_and_massacre" title="1989 Tiananmen Square protests and massacre">Tiananmen Square massacre</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan%27s_political_status" title="Taiwan's political status">Taiwan's political status</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lu_20252_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lu_20252-46"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> DeepSeek models that have been uncensored also display a bias towards Chinese government viewpoints on controversial topics such as <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a>'s human rights record and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan%27s_political_status" title="Taiwan's political status">Taiwan's political status</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> However, users who have downloaded the models and hosted them on their own devices and servers have reported successfully removing this censorship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a class="mw-file-description" href="/wiki/File:DeepSeek_when_asked_about_Xi_Jinping_and_Narendra_Modi.png"><img class="mw-file-element" data-file-height="930" data-file-width="1058" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/DeepSeek_when_asked_about_Xi_Jinping_and_Narendra_Modi.png/250px-DeepSeek_when_asked_about_Xi_Jinping_and_Narendra_Modi.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/DeepSeek_when_asked_about_Xi_Jinping_and_Narendra_Modi.png/500px-DeepSeek_when_asked_about_Xi_Jinping_and_Narendra_Modi.png 1.5x" width="250"/></a><figcaption>Asked if <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a> is an autocrat, DeepSeek apologises that this question is "beyond my current scope". The same question posed about <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">Narendra Modi</a> returns a "balanced analysis" of viewpoints.</figcaption></figure><p> Some sources have observed that the official application programming interface (API) version of R1, which runs from servers located in China, uses censorship mechanisms for topics considered politically sensitive for the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_China" title="Government of China">government of China</a>. For example, the model refuses to answer questions about the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1989_Tiananmen_Square_massacre" title="1989 Tiananmen Square massacre">1989 Tiananmen Square massacre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Uyghurs_in_China" title="Persecution of Uyghurs in China">persecution of Uyghurs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Censorship_of_Winnie-the-Pooh_in_China" title="Censorship of Winnie-the-Pooh in China">comparisons between Xi Jinping and Winnie the Pooh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_China" title="Human rights in China">human rights in China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-52"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tt_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-tt-53"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lu_2025_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lu_2025-54"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Although the AI may initially generate an answer, it then deletes it shortly afterwards and replaces it with a message such as:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tt_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-tt-53"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></p><blockquote><p>"Sorry, that's beyond my current scope. Let's talk about something else."</p></blockquote><p>
The integrated censorship mechanisms and restrictions can only be removed to a limited extent in the open-source version of the R1 model.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-55"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> If the "<a href="/wiki/Core_Socialist_Values" title="Core Socialist Values">core Socialist values</a>" defined by the <a href="/wiki/Cyberspace_Administration_of_China" title="Cyberspace Administration of China">Chinese Internet regulatory authorities</a> are touched on, or the <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">political status of Taiwan</a> is raised, discussions are terminated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Locally hosted instances of R1 are still reported to provide answers consistent with <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chinese Communist Party">Chinese Communist Party</a> <a href="/wiki/Propaganda_in_China" title="Propaganda in China">propaganda</a> narratives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-55"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> When tested by <i><a href="/wiki/NBC_News" title="NBC News">NBC News</a></i>, for instance, DeepSeek's R1 described Taiwan as "an inalienable part of China's territory", and stated:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></p><blockquote><p>"We firmly oppose any form of '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan_independence" title="Taiwan independence">Taiwan independence</a>' separatist activities and are committed to achieving the complete reunification of the motherland through peaceful means."</p></blockquote>
<p>In January 2025, however, Western researchers were able to trick DeepSeek into giving certain answers to some of these topics by requesting in its answer to swap certain letters for <a href="/wiki/Leet" title="Leet">similar-looking numbers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lu_2025_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lu_2025-54"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Security_and_privacy">Security and privacy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Security and privacy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chinese_information_operations_and_information_warfare" title="Chinese information operations and information warfare">Chinese information operations and information warfare</a></div>
<p>Many experts fear that the government of China could use the AI system for foreign <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Influence_operations" title="Influence operations">influence operations</a>, spreading <a href="/wiki/Disinformation" title="Disinformation">disinformation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surveillance" title="Surveillance">surveillance</a>, and the development of <a href="/wiki/Cyberweapon" title="Cyberweapon">cyberweapons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> An article in <i><a href="/wiki/Wired_(magazine)" title="Wired (magazine)">Wired</a></i> commented that the DeepSeek online service sending data to its home country might set "the stage for greater scrutiny".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2025, South Korea's data protection regulator, the <a href="/wiki/Personal_Information_Protection_Commission_(South_Korea)" title="Personal Information Protection Commission (South Korea)">Personal Information Protection Commission</a> (PIPC), raised concerns over DeepSeek, confirming that it sent the nation's user data to the owner of <a href="/wiki/TikTok" title="TikTok">TikTok</a> (<a href="/wiki/ByteDance" title="ByteDance">ByteDance</a>) in China. Accordingly, the PIPC banned new downloads of the app until DeepSeek addressed these concerns. The company's representative in Korea has partially acknowledged its shortcomings in complying with local data protection laws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 29 January 2025, cybersecurity researchers from Wiz Research found a significant data breach at DeepSeek. This occurred due to an improper configuration of a cloud storage database that was left available online without any security precautions.The database at oauth2callback.deepseek.com:9000 and dev.deepseek.com:9000 contained more than a million sensitive entries, which comprised chat messages, API keys, operational details from the backend, system logs, and internal metadata from 6 January 2025. The breach was consequential as it provided complete control over the database, which could lead to unauthorized access and increased privileges within DeepSeeks systems. After Wiz Research reported the issue, DeepSeek secured the database in less than an hour, eliminating any immediate risks. However, the exposure sparked serious concerns about DeepSeeks data security practices and the possibility of facing regulatory action under laws like GDPR or CCPA, particularly if the data included personal information from EU or US residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2025, South Korea's <a href="/wiki/Personal_Information_Protection_Commission_(South_Korea)" title="Personal Information Protection Commission (South Korea)">Personal Information Protection Commission</a> announced that DeepSeek had transferred personal information on over a million South Koreans to China without consent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Miscellaneous">Miscellaneous</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Miscellaneous"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> reported that the DeepSeek app produces instructions for self-harm and dangerous activities more often than its American competitors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Security researchers have found that DeepSeek sends data to a cloud platform affiliated with <a href="/wiki/ByteDance" title="ByteDance">ByteDance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2025, sources claimed that DeepSeek began considering raising external funding for the first time, with Alibaba and Chinese state funds expressing interest in investing in DeepSeek.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On 21 February, DeepSeek announced plans to release key codes and data to the public starting the following week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Restrictions">Restrictions</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Restrictions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Many countries have raised concerns about data security and DeepSeek's use of personal data. On 28 January 2025, the Italian data protection authority announced that it is seeking additional information on DeepSeek's collection and use of personal data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On the same day, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Security_Council" title="United States National Security Council">United States National Security Council</a> announced that it had started a national security review of DeepSeek,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> instructed all its members not to use DeepSeek due to "security and ethical concerns."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On 30 January 2025, Italy's data protection authority, ordered DeepSeek to block its chatbot in the country after the Chinese artificial intelligence startup failed to address the regulator's concerns over its privacy policy. Italian users who downloaded DeepSeek on mobile devices before the ban reported being able to use the chatbot and having access to the web version of DeepSeek after the ban.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Three days later, South Korea's <a href="/wiki/Personal_Information_Protection_Commission_(South_Korea)" title="Personal Information Protection Commission (South Korea)">Personal Information Protection Commission</a> opened an inquiry into DeepSeek's use of personal information;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters-2025_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-2025-78"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Data_Protection_Authority" title="Dutch Data Protection Authority">Dutch Data Protection Authority</a> launched an investigation of DeepSeek;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Taiwan's digital ministry advised its government departments against using the DeepSeek service to "prevent information security risks";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters-2025_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-2025-78"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and  Texas Governor <a href="/wiki/Greg_Abbott" title="Greg Abbott">Greg Abbott</a> issued a state ban on government-issued devices for DeepSeek, along with <a href="/wiki/Xiaohongshu" title="Xiaohongshu">Xiaohongshu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lemon8" title="Lemon8">Lemon8</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2025, access to DeepSeek was banned on the New South Wales <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Customer_Service" title="Department of Customer Service">Department of Customer Service</a>'s devices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> That same month, Australia, South Korea, and Canada banned DeepSeek from government devices,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and South Korea suspended new downloads of DeepSeek due to risks of personal information misuse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In March 2025, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Commerce" title="United States Department of Commerce">U.S. Department of Commerce</a> prohibited DeepSeek on their government devices, due to the danger of disclosing proprietary information with the Chinese Communist Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepSeek_(chatbot)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: See also"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

Parsing

In[29]:
soup = BeautifulSoup(response.content, "html.parser")
In[31]:
title = soup.find("h1").text
print("Page Title:", title)

Page Title: DeepSeek (chatbot)
In[33]:
intro_div = soup.find("div", class_="mw-parser-output")
intro_paragraphs = []
if intro_div:
    for tag in intro_div.find_all("p", recursive=False):
        text = tag.get_text(strip=True)
        if text:
            intro_paragraphs.append(text)
        if len(intro_paragraphs) >= 2:
            break
introduction = "\n\n".join(intro_paragraphs) if intro_paragraphs else "No Introduction"
print("\nIntroduction:\n", introduction)

Introduction:
 DeepSeek[a]is achatbotcreated by the Chinese artificial intelligence companyDeepSeek.

Released on 10 January 2025,DeepSeek-R1surpassedChatGPTas the most downloadedfreewareapp on theiOS App Storein the United States by 27 January.[1]DeepSeek's success against larger and more established rivals has been described as "upending AI"[1]and initiating "a global AIspace race".[2]DeepSeek's compliance with Chinese governmentcensorship policiesand itsdata collection practiceshave also raised concerns over privacy and information control in the model, prompting regulatory scrutiny in multiple countries. However, it has also been praised for its open weights and infrastructure code, energy efficiency and contributions to theopen-source community.[3][4]

        print(f"Section Title: {section_title}")
        print(f"Section Content: {section_content[:300]}...")
        print()

Fetch the section History

In[49]:
headers = soup.find_all(['h2', 'h3'])

# Iterate through headers to find the "History" section
history_section_found = False
for header in headers:
    if header.get_text(strip=True).lower() == 'history':
        history_section_found = True
        # Start extracting paragraphs after the "History" header
        next_node = header.find_next()
        while next_node and next_node.name not in ['h2', 'h3']:
            if next_node.name == 'p':
                print(next_node.get_text())
            next_node = next_node.find_next()

if not history_section_found:
    print("History section not found.")

On 10 January 2025, DeepSeek released the chatbot, based on the DeepSeek-R1 model, for iOS and Android. By 27 January, DeepSeek-R1 surpassed ChatGPT as the most-downloaded freeware app on the iOS App Store in the United States,[1] which resulted in an 18% drop in Nvidias share price.[5][6] After a "large-scale" cyberattack on the same day disrupted the proper functioning of its servers, DeepSeek limited its new user registration to phone numbers from mainland China, email addresses, or Google account logins.[7][8]

On 3 April 2025, in collaboration with researchers at Tsinghua University, DeepSeek published a paper unveiling a new model that combines the techniques generative reward modeling (GRM) and self-principled critique tuning (SPCT). The resulting model is referred to as DeepSeek-GRM. The goal of using these techniques is to foster more effective inference-time scaling within their LLM and chatbot services. Notably DeepSeek has said that these new models will be released and made open source.[9][10]

On 30 April 2025, Deepseek released its math-focused Artificial Intelligence Model named "DeepSeek-Prover-V2-671B". This Model is useful for formal theorem proving and mathematical reasoning.[11][12]

    href = link.get("href")
    if href:

Sentiment analysis

In[73]:
from textblob import TextBlob
In[75]:
# Get the page text
page_text = soup.get_text()

# Step 3: Clean up the extracted text (optional)
# Remove extra newlines and spaces
page_text = ' '.join(page_text.split())

# Step 4: Perform Sentiment Analysis with TextBlob
blob = TextBlob(page_text)

# Step 5: Output the sentiment analysis results
print("Sentiment Analysis Result:")
print(f"Polarity: {blob.sentiment.polarity}")  # Range: -1 (negative) to 1 (positive)
print(f"Subjectivity: {blob.sentiment.subjectivity}")  # Range: 0 (objective) to 1 (subjective)

Sentiment Analysis Result:
Polarity: 0.09721527198591419
Subjectivity: 0.3768874856030817

Polarity: 0.097 The sentiment of the entire article is slightly positive, but not very strong. A polarity close to 0 means it's fairly neutral, with a slight tendency toward positive sentiment.

Subjectivity: 0.377 The article is somewhat objective (close to 0), with some level of subjectivity, as expected for a Wikipedia page. This indicates that the article contains a mix of factual content and potentially opinion-based information.
